rainerscript: random() function does not provide user-visible warning when passed an unsupported value
### Expected behavior

1. Call `random()` function a value larger than what the underlying platform supports
1. A warning is emitted to debug and "normal" output

### Actual behavior

1. Call `random()` function a value larger than what the underlying platform supports
1. A warning is emitted to debug output only

### Steps to reproduce the behavior

1. Build current master
1. Enable debug logging
1. Call the `random()` function with a value larger than the platform supports

Here's the result of running `cat -n` on /testbed/runtime/errmsg.c:
    70	
    71	int hadErrMsgs(void) {
    72	    return bHadErrMsgs;
    73	}
    74	
    75	/* We now receive three parameters: one is the internal error code
    76	 * which will also become the error message number, the second is
    77	 * errno - if it is non-zero, the corresponding error message is included
    78	 * in the text and finally the message text itself. Note that it is not
    79	 * 100% clean to use the internal errcode, as it may be reached from
    80	 * multiple actual error causes. However, it is much better than having
    81	 * no error code at all (and in most cases, a single internal error code
    82	 * maps to a specific error event).
    83	 * rgerhards, 2008-06-27
    84	 */
    85	static void doLogMsg(const int iErrno, const int iErrCode, const int severity, const char *msg) {
    86	    char buf[2048];
    87	    char errStr[1024];
    88	
    89	    dbgprintf("Called LogMsg, msg: %s\n", msg);
    90	    osf_write(OSF_TAG_MSG, msg);
    91	
    92	    if (iErrno != 0) {
    93	        rs_strerror_r(iErrno, errStr, sizeof(errStr));
    94	        if (iErrCode == NO_ERRCODE || iErrCode == RS_RET_ERR) {
    95	            snprintf(buf, sizeof(buf), "%s: %s [v%s]", msg, errStr, VERSION);
    96	        } else {
    97	            snprintf(buf, sizeof(buf), "%s: %s [v%s try https://www.rsyslog.com/e/%d ]", msg, errStr, VERSION,
    98	                     iErrCode * -1);
    99	        }
   100	    } else {
   101	        if (iErrCode == NO_ERRCODE || iErrCode == RS_RET_ERR) {
   102	            snprintf(buf, sizeof(buf), "%s [v%s]", msg, VERSION);
   103	        } else {
   104	            snprintf(buf, sizeof(buf), "%s [v%s try https://www.rsyslog.com/e/%d ]", msg, VERSION, iErrCode * -1);
   105	        }
   106	    }
   107	    buf[sizeof(buf) - 1] = '\0'; /* just to be on the safe side... */
   108	    errno = 0;
   109	
   110	    const int msglen = (int)strlen(buf);
   111	    if (msglen > glblGetMaxLine(ourConf)) {
   112	        /* in extreme cases, our error messages may be longer than the configured
   113	         * max message size. If so, we just truncate without further indication, as
   114	         * anything else would probably lead to a death loop on error messages.
   115	         * Note that we do not split, as we really do not anticipate there is
   116	         * much value in supporting extremely short max message sizes - we assume
   117	         * it's just a testbench thing. -- rgerhards, 2018-05-11
   118	         */
   119	        buf[glblGetMaxLine(ourConf)] = '\0'; /* space must be available! */
   120	    }
   121	
   122	    glblErrLogger(severity, iErrCode, (uchar *)buf);
   123	
   124	    if (severity == LOG_ERR) bHadErrMsgs = 1;
   125	}
   126	
   127	/* We now receive three parameters: one is the internal error code
   128	 * which will also become the error message number, the second is
   129	 * errno - if it is non-zero, the corresponding error message is included
   130	 * in the text and finally the message text itself. Note that it is not
   131	 * 100% clean to use the internal errcode, as it may be reached from
   132	 * multiple actual error causes. However, it is much better than having
   133	 * no error code at all (and in most cases, a single internal error code
   134	 * maps to a specific error event).
   135	 * rgerhards, 2008-06-27
   136	 */
   137	void __attribute__((format(printf, 3, 4))) LogError(const int iErrno, const int iErrCode, const char *fmt, ...) {
   138	    va_list ap;
   139	    char buf[2048];
   140	    int lenBuf;
   141	
   142	    va_start(ap, fmt);
   143	    lenBuf = vsnprintf(buf, sizeof(buf), fmt, ap);
   144	    if (lenBuf < 0) {
   145	        strncpy(buf, "error message lost due to problem with vsnprintf", sizeof(buf));
   146	    }
   147	    va_end(ap);
   148	    buf[sizeof(buf) - 1] = '\0'; /* just to be on the safe side... */
   149	
   150	    doLogMsg(iErrno, iErrCode, LOG_ERR, buf);
   151	}
   152	
   153	/* We now receive three parameters: one is the internal error code
   154	 * which will also become the error message number, the second is
   155	 * errno - if it is non-zero, the corresponding error message is included
   156	 * in the text and finally the message text itself. Note that it is not
   157	 * 100% clean to use the internal errcode, as it may be reached from
   158	 * multiple actual error causes. However, it is much better than having
   159	 * no error code at all (and in most cases, a single internal error code
   160	 * maps to a specific error event).
   161	 * rgerhards, 2008-06-27
   162	 */
   163	void __attribute__((format(printf, 4, 5))) LogMsg(
   164	    const int iErrno, const int iErrCode, const int severity, const char *fmt, ...) {
   165	    va_list ap;
   166	    char buf[2048];
   167	    int lenBuf;
   168	
   169	    va_start(ap, fmt);
   170	    lenBuf = vsnprintf(buf, sizeof(buf), fmt, ap);
   171	    if (lenBuf < 0) {
   172	        strncpy(buf, "error message lost due to problem with vsnprintf", sizeof(buf));
   173	    }
   174	    va_end(ap);
   175	    buf[sizeof(buf) - 1] = '\0'; /* just to be on the safe side... */
   176	
   177	    doLogMsg(iErrno, iErrCode, severity, buf);
   178	}
   179	
   180	
   181	/* Write an oversize message to the oversize message error log.
   182	 * We do NOT handle errors during writing that log other than emitting
   183	 * yet another error message. The reason is that there really is nothing
   184	 * else that we could do in that case.
   185	 * rgerhards, 2018-05-03

#!/bin/bash
set -euo pipefail
work=$(mktemp -d /tmp/rsyslog-random-repro.XXXXXX)
cd /testbed/tests
cat > "$work/random.conf" <<CONF
module(load="../plugins/imdiag/.libs/imdiag")
global(debug.abortOnProgramError="on")
\$IMDiagListenPortFileName $work/imdiag.port
\$IMDiagServerRun 0

template(name="outfmt" type="string" string="%\$.random_no%\n")
set \$.random_no = random(9223372036854775807);
action(type="omfile" file="$work/out.log" template="outfmt")
CONF
RSYSLOG_DEBUG="debug nologfuncflow noprintmutexaction" RSYSLOG_DEBUGLOG="$work/debug.log" \
  ../tools/rsyslogd -C -n -i"$work/pid" -M../runtime/.libs:../.libs -f"$work/random.conf" >"$work/stdout.log" 2>"$work/stderr.log" &
pid=$!
for i in {1..100}; do [ -s "$work/imdiag.port" ] && break; sleep 0.1; done
port=$(cat "$work/imdiag.port")
echo 'injectmsg literal <167>Mar  1 01:00:00 host tag msg' | ./diagtalker -p"$port" >/dev/null
for i in {1..50}; do [ -s "$work/out.log" ] && break; sleep 0.1; done
echo WaitMainQueueEmpty | ./diagtalker -p"$port" >/dev/null || true
kill "$pid" 2>/dev/null || true
wait "$pid" 2>/dev/null || true
printf 'WORKDIR=%s\n' "$work"
printf '\n--- debug warning ---\n'
grep -h "desired random-number range" "$work/debug.log" || true
printf '\n--- normal output warning ---\n'
grep -h "desired random-number range" "$work/stdout.log" "$work/stderr.log" || true
EOF

     2	 * This file set implements the internal messages input module for rsyslog.
     3	 * Note: we currently do not have an input module spec, but

    42	static linkedList_t llMsgs;
    43	static pthread_mutex_t mutList = PTHREAD_MUTEX_INITIALIZER;
    44	
    45	
    46	/* destructs an iminternal object
    47	 */
    48	static rsRetVal iminternalDestruct(iminternal_t *pThis) {
    49	    DEFiRet;
    50	
    51	    if (pThis->pMsg != NULL) msgDestruct(&pThis->pMsg);
    52	
    53	    free(pThis);
    54	
    55	    RETiRet;
    56	}
    57	
    58	
    59	/* Construct an iminternal object
    60	 */
    61	static rsRetVal iminternalConstruct(iminternal_t **ppThis) {
    62	    DEFiRet;
    63	    if ((*ppThis = (iminternal_t *)calloc(1, sizeof(iminternal_t))) == NULL) {
    64	        iRet = RS_RET_OUT_OF_MEMORY;
    65	    }
    66	    RETiRet;
    67	}
    68	
    69	
    70	/* add a message to the linked list
    71	 * Note: the pMsg reference counter is not incremented. Consequently,
    72	 * the caller must NOT decrement it. The caller actually hands over
    73	 * full ownership of the pMsg object.
    74	 */
    75	rsRetVal iminternalAddMsg(smsg_t *pMsg) {
    76	    DEFiRet;
    77	    iminternal_t *pThis = NULL;
    78	    struct timespec to;
    79	    int r;
    80	    int is_locked = 0;
    81	
    82	    /* we guard against deadlock, so we can guarantee rsyslog will never
    83	     * block due to internal messages. The 1 second timeout should be
    84	     * sufficient under all circumstances.
    85	     */
    86	    to.tv_sec = time(NULL) + 1;
    87	    to.tv_nsec = 0;
    88	#if !defined(__APPLE__)
    89	    r = pthread_mutex_timedlock(&mutList, &to);
    90	#else
    91	    r = pthread_mutex_trylock(&mutList);  // must check
    92	#endif
    93	    if (r != 0) {
    94	        dbgprintf("iminternalAddMsg: timedlock for mutex failed with %d, msg %s\n", r, getMSG(pMsg));
    95	        /* the message is lost, nothing we can do against this! */
    96	        msgDestruct(&pMsg);
    97	        ABORT_FINALIZE(RS_RET_ERR);
    98	    }
    99	    is_locked = 1;
   100	    CHKiRet(iminternalConstruct(&pThis));
   101	    pThis->pMsg = pMsg;
   102	    CHKiRet(llAppend(&llMsgs, NULL, (void *)pThis));
   103	
   104	    if (PREFER_FETCH_32BIT(bHaveMainQueue)) {
   105	        DBGPRINTF("signaling new internal message via SIGTTOU: '%s'\n", pThis->pMsg->pszRawMsg);
   106	        kill(glblGetOurPid(), SIGTTOU);
   107	    }
   108	
   109	finalize_it:
   110	    if (is_locked) {
   111	        pthread_mutex_unlock(&mutList);
   112	    }
   113	    if (iRet != RS_RET_OK) {
   114	        dbgprintf("iminternalAddMsg() error %d - can not otherwise report this error, message lost\n", iRet);
   115	        if (pThis != NULL) iminternalDestruct(pThis);
   116	    }
   117	
   118	    RETiRet;
   119	}
   120	
   121	
   122	/* pull the first error message from the linked list, remove it
   123	 * from the list and return it to the caller. The caller is
   124	 * responsible for freeing the message!
   125	 */
   126	rsRetVal iminternalRemoveMsg(smsg_t **ppMsg) {
   127	    DEFiRet;
   128	    iminternal_t *pThis;
   129	    linkedListCookie_t llCookie = NULL;
   130	
   131	    pthread_mutex_lock(&mutList);
   132	    CHKiRet(llGetNextElt(&llMsgs, &llCookie, (void *)&pThis));
   133	    if (!strcmp((char *)pThis->pMsg->pszHOSTNAME, "[localhost]")) {
   134	        /* early (pre-conf) startup message detected, need to set real hostname now */
   135	        MsgSetHOSTNAME(pThis->pMsg, glblGetLocalHostName(), ustrlen(glblGetLocalHostName()));
   136	    }
   137	    *ppMsg = pThis->pMsg;
   138	    pThis->pMsg = NULL; /* we do no longer own it - important for destructor */
   139	
   140	    if (llDestroyRootElt(&llMsgs) != RS_RET_OK) {

#!/bin/bash
set -euo pipefail
work=$(mktemp -d /tmp/rsyslog-random-repro.XXXXXX)
cd /testbed/tests
cat > "$work/random.conf" <<CONF
module(load="../plugins/imdiag/.libs/imdiag")
global(debug.abortOnProgramError="on")
\$IMDiagListenPortFileName $work/imdiag.port
\$IMDiagServerRun 0

template(name="msgonly" type="string" string="%msg%\n")
template(name="outfmt" type="string" string="%\$.random_no%\n")
if \$syslogtag contains "rsyslogd" then action(type="omfile" file="$work/warn.log" template="msgonly")
if \$msg contains "trigger_random" then {
  set \$.random_no = random(9223372036854775807);
  action(type="omfile" file="$work/out.log" template="outfmt")
}
CONF
RSYSLOG_DEBUG="debug nostdout" RSYSLOG_DEBUGLOG="$work/debug.log" \
  ../tools/rsyslogd -C -n -i"$work/pid" -M../runtime/.libs:../.libs -f"$work/random.conf" >"$work/stdout.log" 2>"$work/stderr.log" &

wait "$pid" 2>/dev/null || true

  1905	/* rsyslogdDoDie() is a signal handler. If called, it sets the bFinished variable
  1906	 * to indicate the program should terminate. However, it does not terminate
  1907	 * it itself, because that causes issues with multi-threading. The actual
  1908	 * termination is then done on the main thread. This solution might introduce
  1909	 * a minimal delay, but it is much cleaner than the approach of doing everything
  1910	 * inside the signal handler.
  1911	 * rgerhards, 2005-10-26
  1912	 * Note:
  1913	 * - we do not call DBGPRINTF() as this may cause us to block in case something
  1914	 *   with the threading is wrong.
  1915	 * - we do not really care about the return state of write(), but we need this
  1916	 *   strange check we do to silence compiler warnings (thanks, Ubuntu!)
  1917	 */
  1918	void rsyslogdDoDie(int sig) {
  1919	#define MSG1 "DoDie called.\n"
  1920	#define MSG2 "DoDie called 5 times - unconditional exit\n"
  1921	    static int iRetries = 0; /* debug aid */
  1922	    dbgprintf(MSG1);
  1923	    if (Debug == DEBUG_FULL) {
  1924	        if (write(1, MSG1, sizeof(MSG1) - 1) == -1) {
  1925	            dbgprintf("%s:%d: write failed\n", __FILE__, __LINE__);
  1926	        }
  1927	    }
  1928	    if (iRetries++ == 4) {
  1929	        if (Debug == DEBUG_FULL) {
  1930	            if (write(1, MSG2, sizeof(MSG2) - 1) == -1) {
  1931	                dbgprintf("%s:%d: write failed\n", __FILE__, __LINE__);
  1932	            }
  1933	        }
  1934	        abort();
  1935	    }
  1936	    bFinished = sig;
  1937	    if (runConf && runConf->globals.debugOnShutdown) {
  1938	        /* kind of hackish - set to 0, so that debug_swith will enable
  1939	         * and AND emit the "start debug log" message.
  1940	         */
  1941	        debugging_on = 0;
  1942	        rsyslogdDebugSwitch();
  1943	    }
  1944	#undef MSG1
  1945	#undef MSG2

cat > /tmp/repro_random_warning2.sh <<'EOF'
#!/bin/bash
set -euo pipefail
work=$(mktemp -d /tmp/rsyslog-random-repro.XXXXXX)
cd /testbed/tests
cat > "$work/random.conf" <<CONF
module(load="../plugins/imdiag/.libs/imdiag")
global(debug.abortOnProgramError="on")
\$IMDiagListenPortFileName $work/imdiag.port
\$IMDiagServerRun 0

template(name="msgonly" type="string" string="%syslogtag%|%msg%\n")
template(name="outfmt" type="string" string="%\$.random_no%\n")
action(type="omfile" file="$work/all.log" template="msgonly")
if \$msg contains "trigger_random" then {
  set \$.random_no = random(9223372036854775807);
  action(type="omfile" file="$work/out.log" template="outfmt")
}
CONF
RSYSLOG_DEBUG="debug nostdout" RSYSLOG_DEBUGLOG="$work/debug.log" \
  ../tools/rsyslogd -C -n -i"$work/pid" -M../runtime/.libs:../.libs -f"$work/random.conf" >"$work/stdout.log" 2>"$work/stderr.log" &
pid=$!
for i in {1..100}; do [ -s "$work/imdiag.port" ] && break; sleep 0.1; done
port=$(cat "$work/imdiag.port")
echo 'injectmsg literal <167>Mar  1 01:00:00 host tag trigger_random' | ./diagtalker -p"$port" >/dev/null
for i in {1..100}; do grep -q "desired random-number range" "$work/all.log" 2>/dev/null && break; sleep 0.1; done
echo WaitMainQueueEmpty | ./diagtalker -p"$port" >/dev/null || true
sleep 0.2
kill "$pid" 2>/dev/null || true
wait "$pid" 2>/dev/null || true
printf 'WORKDIR=%s\n' "$work"
printf '\n--- debug warning ---\n'
grep -h "desired random-number range" "$work/debug.log" || true
printf '\n--- normal all file ---\n'
grep -h "desired random-number range" "$work/all.log" || true
EOF
chmod +x /tmp/repro_random_warning2.sh

   884	/* this is a special function used to submit an error message. This
   885	 * function is also passed to the runtime library as the generic error
   886	 * message handler. -- rgerhards, 2008-04-17
   887	 */
   888	void rsyslogd_submitErrMsg(const int severity, const int iErr, const uchar *msg) {
   889	    if (glbl.GetGlobalInputTermState() == 1) {
   890	        /* After fork the stderr is unusable (dfltErrLogger uses is internally) */
   891	        if (!doFork) dfltErrLogger(severity, iErr, msg);
   892	    } else {
   893	        logmsgInternal(iErr, LOG_SYSLOG | (severity & 0x07), msg, 0);
   894	    }
   895	}
